### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you typically need to follow a specific process outlined by your university. Here's a general guide on how to proceed:

1. **Meet with your Academic Advisor**: The first step is to discuss your interest in changing your major with your current academic advisor. They can provide guidance on the process and requirements specific to your institution.

2. **Research the New Major**: Before formally applying to change your major, research the new field of study to ensure it aligns with your interests and career goals. Understand the prerequisites, courses, and any additional requirements for the new major.

3. **Complete the Necessary Forms**: Most universities require you to fill out a formal application or petition to change your major. This form usually asks for your current major, the new major you wish to pursue, and may require a statement of purpose explaining your reasons for the change.

4. **Gather Supporting Documents**: Depending on the university's requirements, you may need to provide supporting documents such as transcripts, letters of recommendation, or a resume detailing your academic and extracurricular achievements.

5. **Get Approval from the Department**: The department of the new major may require an interview or a meeting with a faculty member to discuss your academic background and suitability for the new major.

6. **Get Approval from the Registrar’s Office**: Once your application is approved by the department, it must be submitted to and approved by the Registrar’s Office to officially change your major on your academic record.

7. **Consult with Financial Aid**: If you receive financial aid, changing your major could affect your aid package. It’s important to consult with the financial aid office to understand how the change might impact your funding.

8. **Consider Implications**: Changing your major can have various implications, including additional coursework, different graduation requirements, and potential impacts on your academic and career plans. Make sure to consider these carefully.

9. **Stay Informed**: Keep yourself informed about the deadlines and any additional steps required by your university. Some institutions may have specific deadlines for changing majors, and missing these could delay the process.

Remember, the exact process can vary significantly from one institution to another, so it's crucial to consult the specific guidelines and requirements provided by your university. The documents you provided (the Transfer SME form and the Petition for Alternative Course Load form) do not directly relate to changing your major, but they do illustrate the formal processes involved in academic administration at a university.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions.

After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. ### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross-listed or tagged courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. Additionally, students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses) in each of the three exploratory categories (E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM) for a total of 24 exploratory credits (6 courses). The core courses requirement is 20 credits (5 courses). Therefore, the total number of courses a student can take, considering all these requirements, is 6 (Exploratory) + 5 (Core) + up to 6 (double-counted courses for majors/minors) = 17 courses. However, this is a maximum and assumes the student takes the maximum allowable double-counted courses and completes all requirements for each major and the exploratory categories. The actual number of courses will depend on the specific distribution of courses chosen by the student to meet their major requirements, which could be more or fewer than the maximum calculated here.

### Question 56: How many courses in a semester can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The passage does not specify the maximum number of courses a student can take in a semester. It provides information about major and minor requirements, Exploratory requirements, and rules for double majors and minors, but it does not address the total number of courses a student can take in a semester. Therefore, the answer to the question is that the passage does not provide this information. Students should refer to their university's academic calendar or consult with their academic advisor for information on course load limits per semester.

### Question 58: How can I audit a course?  
### Answer: 

Auditing a course is not typically an option at most institutions, including the one described in the given context. The provided document outlines the process for applying for Credit Transfer and Exemptions, as well as the policies for transferring credits from A-level, AP, IB, and CIE courses. It also discusses the procedures for handling excused absences due to personal emergencies or approved trips, and the responsibilities of instructors regarding attendance policies.

The document does not mention auditing a course, which is a non-credit option where students attend classes but do not receive a grade or academic credit. Auditing a course usually requires permission from the instructor and sometimes the department or registrar's office, and it may have different rules and requirements compared to taking a course for credit.

To audit a course, a student would typically need to:

1. Contact the instructor of the course to express their interest in auditing.
2. Obtain the instructor's permission to audit the course.
3. Complete any necessary paperwork, which may include a form available from the registrar's office.
4. Pay any applicable audit fees, if they exist.

However, since the document does not mention auditing, it is best to refer to the institution's official academic catalog or contact the registrar's office directly for specific information on auditing courses at the institution in question.

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

The maximum number of courses that can be double-counted for a double major is 8 credits (2 courses). This limit applies per each pair of majors and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim overall. For example, a student majoring in both A and B and minoring in C can have a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. However, this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged.

### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

At Fulbright, the majority of courses apply a standard letter grade ranging from ‘A’ to ‘F.’ Grade points are assigned to letter grades according to the following scale (unless otherwise decided by faculty in individual courses): Letter Grade Grade Point Grade Category Percentage A 4.0 90-100 B 3.0 80-89 C 2.0 70-79 D 1.0 60-69 F 0.0 Below 60

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
The final grade for the thesis is the average of the 2 graders. The oral defense is graded by a panel of all IS faculty. See Appendix 1and 2 for detail rubrics on both the thesis and presentation. The total grade of the capstone is the sum of the thesis grade and oral defense grade. The primary advisor will communicate this result and any feedback from the graders to the student in writing. If there are any concerns about the grades, students should first meet with their primary advisor to discuss and clarify. If no agreement is made, the student could request one more grader (an IS faculty) to grade their submission, but cannot choose who the grader would be. The major coordinator will decide the 3rd grader after discussion with IS faculty team. The new grade would be the average of the 3 graders. Any further appeal after this would need to follow official UG program’s process for grade appeal.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you failed to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The process involves the following steps:

1. **Academic Warning**: Initially, you receive official warnings for academic performance issues.
2. **Academic Probation**: After three official warnings, you are placed on Academic Probation, which is the second level of intervention.
3. **Failure to Meet Requirements**: If you fail to meet all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation, you may require an additional Academic Progress Meeting.
4. **Academic Suspension**: If you continue to fail to meet the requirements, you may be placed on Academic Suspension. This is entered on your transcript as part of your academic record.
5. **Meeting with the Dean’s Office**: The suspended student must meet with the Dean’s Office to establish the conditions that must be met prior to returning to Fulbright.
6. **Conditions for Return**: While on suspension, you may not visit the Fulbright campus without permission from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for attending relevant meetings. The suspension typically lasts for one term or one academic year.
7. **Maximum Suspensions**: You may be suspended a maximum of two times. A third suspension will result in the cancellation of your enrolment in the program.
8. **Application for Re-admission**: After a cancellation, you must apply for re-admission. Your application must include a letter addressing the reasons for your suspensions and cancellations, along with measures you have taken to address those issues.
9. **Re-admission Decision**: The Dean’s Office, in consultation with faculty and staff, will make the re-admission decision.

The key to avoiding academic suspension is to meet all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. This typically involves improving your academic performance, seeking academic support, and adhering to the conditions set by the Dean’s Office if you are placed on probation or suspension.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. 6.3 Academic Probation This is the second level of intervention. It is intended to make students aware that their academic performance puts them at risk of losing the opportunity to study at Fulbright, either temporarily (Suspension) or permanently (Dismissal). Students on Academic Warning who fail to meet all the requirements of their Learning Contract may require an additional Academic Progress Meeting and may be placed on Academic Probation, typically resulting in an updated Learning Contract. Suspensions typically are for one term or one academic year. A student may be suspended a maximum of two times. A student will not be suspended a third time but will instead

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
student must meet with the Dean’s Office, who establishes the conditions that the student must meet prior to returning to Fulbright. While on suspension, a student may not visit the Fulbright campus unless permission is given from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions typically are for one term or one academic year. A student may be suspended a maximum of two times. A student will not be suspended a third time but will instead have their enrolment in the program canceled. A student in this situation must apply for re-admission. The student must include with his or her application for re-admission a letter that addresses the reasons for their suspensions and cancellation, and the measures they have taken to address those reasons. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. Students who are re-admitted must also re- apply for financial aid.  

</details> 

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

Students can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. They must complete a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submit it to the Registrar’s Office before a specific deadline (4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term). Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the grade to P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, and courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and these courses can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. However, Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. The NP grade will be shown on the official transcript, but it does not contribute to the GPA. Only the Pass grades contribute to the GPA.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

The failed course will count toward the total attempted credits, but it will not count toward the 144 maximum credits you can have if you repeat it and receive a passing grade. When you repeat a course and receive a higher grade, the failed grade is replaced with an "RP" notation, meaning "repeated", and only the higher grade is used in the GPA calculation. Therefore, the failed course does not contribute to the 144 maximum credits, as long as you successfully repeat it and improve your grade. However, it's important to note that you cannot repeat the same course for a third time unless you failed the second attempt or if a specific grade is required to meet major requirements. Always consult with your Academic/Major Advisor for guidance on your program plan, especially when considering repeating courses.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. To receive an Academic Warning, the Registrar’s Office sends out the warning. The student is then required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.  

<details>

### Question 67: How can I make reservations of rooms for personal usage?  
### Answer: 

You cannot make reservations of rooms for personal usage. Room reservations are typically handled by the Residential Life office or a similar department. To make a reservation, you should contact the appropriate office and follow their procedures for reserving space. This may involve filling out a form, providing a reason for the reservation, and possibly paying a fee. It is important to check the specific policies of your institution as they may vary. Additionally, remember to adhere to any rules and regulations set forth by the institution regarding room usage.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, you should consider taking a combination of Pure Mathematics courses, Intermediate Courses, Advanced Courses, and Elective Applied courses. Here are some suggested courses:

Intermediate Courses:
- Probability
- Differential Equations
- Discrete Mathematics
- Numerical Analysis

Advanced Courses:
- Advanced Statistics
- Statistical Learning
- Stochastic Calculus
- Numerical Analysis
- Optimization
- Partial Differential Equations

Pure Mathematics Courses:
- Abstract Algebra
- Real Analysis

Elective Applied Courses:
- Sample Applied Courses from other majors could include:
  - Game theory (Economics)
  - The Economics of Corruption (Economics)
  - Money and Banking (Economics)
  - Economics of Inequality (Economics)
  - Signal processing (Engineering)
  - Numerical simulation (Engineering)
  - Inverse problems (Engineering)
  - Machine learning (Data Science)
  - Artificial intelligence (Data Science)

Remember to consult with an academic advisor to tailor your course selection to your interests and career goals within the Applied Mathematics field. Additionally, participation in research seminars and a capstone project can provide valuable research experience and help you develop essential skills for a career in mathematics or its applications.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 17]

Consultation with an academic advisor is required for course selection. Sample Advanced Courses • Advanced Statistics • Statistical Learning • Stochastic Calculus • Numerical Analysis • Optimization • Partial Differential Equations Elective Applied courses: These are the courses from other majors that emphasize the applications of Mathematics. ### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) requires all full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students to complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. This program is designed to facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty.

However, the information provided does not directly address how a student can receive a subsidy for not being paid by the company they are working with under the General Work Program for Experiential Learning. Typically, subsidies or financial support for ELP might be available through the university, but the specific details on eligibility, application, and the amount of subsidy would be outlined in the ELP guidelines or through direct communication with the university's financial aid or ELP office.

To inquire about a subsidy, a student should:

1. Review the ELP guidelines and any related financial aid information available on the Fulbright University website or through the One Stop portal.
2. Contact the ELP coordinator or the financial aid office at Fulbright University to discuss their specific situation and inquire about potential subsidies or financial support options.
3. Provide any necessary documentation, such as a letter from the company stating the lack of payment, to support their application for financial aid or subsidy.
4. Follow the application process for financial aid or subsidy as outlined by the university.

It is important to note that while the university may offer support, the availability and terms of such support can vary, and students should be prepared to provide evidence of their financial need and the circumstances surrounding their unpaid work placement.

### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The Capstone process typically begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II. Here's a step-by-step guide to completing a Capstone project:

**General Information:**
- The Capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of your curriculum.
- It can draw from extra-curricular activities and practical experience.
- The project should evidence competency in a primary disciplinary specialization, optionally supported by secondary and tertiary areas.
- In the Art & Media Studies major, it could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. For other majors, consult with prospective advisors early in your junior year.

**Planning:**
- Carefully consider the project idea, ensuring it demonstrates original critical and creative thinking.
- Encourage primary research but avoid extensive fieldwork.
- Plan the scope and feasibility of the project with your advisor(s).

**Capstone I:**
- Meet with your advisor early in the semester to set a regular meeting schedule and expectations.
- Complete a literature review or annotated bibliography of at least five pages (2,000 words) or an introduction, and other materials as agreed upon with your advisors.
- Regularly update your advisors on your progress.

**Capstone II:**
- Focus on production, whether it's writing your thesis or realizing a creative project.
- Continue to work closely with your advisors, updating them on your progress and seeking feedback.
- The end product should be a coherent and meaningful representation of your learning and research.

**Completion:**
- The Capstone culminates in a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers.
- The project should be original, demonstrate critical and creative thinking, and be a testament to your academic and practical skills.

**Note:** The format and length of projects are flexible within certain limits, and students work with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. It's important to stay in regular communication with your advisors and to plan your project carefully to ensure a successful completion.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! ### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

To get a distinctive graduation, students must maintain a Grade Point Average (GPA) that is calculated by dividing [the sum of (grade points earned * credit hours earned) for each course] by [the total attempted credits for GPA]. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

An honour pass capstone is the key requirement for graduating with Honor. You must maintain a 3.6 GPA throughout your senior year to be able to earn an Honors for the capstone. Failure to maintain the required GPA will result in the capstone being capped at Pass.

### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of absences: General absences, Military leave, and Excused absence due to university-sponsored events/activities.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have one, you must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, along with any required supporting documents, before the last day of class. For Personal Leave, you must be in Good Academic Standing and apply for one to two terms. For Medical Leave, you must submit the form along with a Fulbright Impact Assessment form and all medical supporting documents. The leave duration is determined in conjunction with a health services professional, the Registrar’s Office, and the student. Administrative Leave of Absence may be placed on you if you have an outstanding student account balance without informing the school.

LEAVE OF ABSENCE: Students who wish to take a period of leave from their studies at Fulbright must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form , along with supporting documents, before the last day of class. Fulbright permits students in Good Academic Standing to apply for a leave of absence for one to two terms. Normally, a student is not permitted to remain on campus during a period of absence from their studies. Students may return earlier to Fulbright by notifying the Registrar’s Office at least eight (08) weeks in advance of the returning term. Students who return and resume their studies at Fulbright are expected to complete their program without further interruption. ### Question 77: How can I report violation of Academic environment anonymously?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University Vietnam has a clear policy on academic integrity and expects all students to adhere to these standards. If you witness a violation of academic integrity or any other academic misconduct, you can report it anonymously through the university's designated channels. Typically, universities have a confidential reporting system in place where individuals can report concerns without revealing their identity. This system is usually managed by the Office of Academic Affairs or the Office of Student Conduct. Here's how you might proceed:

1. **Contact the Office of Academic Affairs**: Reach out to the Office of Academic Affairs and express your concern about the violation of academic integrity. They can guide you on how to report the incident anonymously.

2. **Use the University's Reporting System**: Many universities have an online reporting system or a hotline where you can submit a report. This system is designed to protect the identity of the reporter.

3. **Submit a Written Report**: If there is no online system, you can write a detailed report describing the incident, including dates, times, locations, and any evidence you have gathered. You can submit this report to the Office of Academic Affairs or the Office of Student Conduct in a sealed envelope to maintain anonymity.

4. **Follow Up**: After submitting your report, it's important to follow up with the relevant office to ensure that your report has been received and is being investigated.

5. **Maintain Confidentiality**: Even if you choose to remain anonymous, it's important to avoid discussing the incident with others to protect your identity and the integrity of the investigation.

Remember, the goal is to uphold academic integrity and ensure a fair and respectful learning environment for all students. Reporting violations, even anonymously, is a responsible action that contributes to maintaining academic standards at the university.

### Question 78: Where can I get all forms and pdf related to my academic journey at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

At the end of each term, grade reports are available for viewing on the Fulbright One Stop portal, named Unofficial Transcript. Paper copies of grade reports, named Transcript of Records, can be issued by the Registrar’s Office upon students' request. Additionally, forms such as the Incomplete Grade Request form and Leave of Absence documentation can be obtained from the respective offices (Academic Affairs and Residential Life) or their online portals.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic integrity is outlined in the Academic Integrity section of their guidelines. The first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress, including those who have committed academic integrity violations, is an Academic Warning. This warning is issued by the Registrar’s Office and requires the student to attend an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract is created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. If a student receives three official warnings, they may face disciplinary action, which could result in Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

The second level of intervention is Academic Probation, which is intended to make students aware that their academic performance is at risk. Students on Academic Warning who fail to meet all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Probation, resulting in an updated Learning Contract. Academic Probation typically lasts for a term.

A student on Academic Probation who fails to fulfill all the requirements of their Learning Contract may be placed on Academic Suspension. Suspensions are recorded on the student’s transcript and can result in the temporary loss of the opportunity to study at the institution.

In summary, the school takes academic integrity violations seriously and handles them through a progressive disciplinary process that starts with an Academic Warning and can lead to Academic Probation or Suspension if the violations are not addressed. Three official warnings can result in disciplinary action, and the Registrar's Office is involved in monitoring and following up on these cases.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

Students are required to repeat core courses in the case of receiving the grade F and/or course(s) counted toward major/minor in the case of receiving a grade below ‘C-’. Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a ‘D+’ following consultation with the student’s academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the course twice. The GPA is calculated by dividing the sum of (grade points earned * credit hours earned) for each course by the total attempted credits for GPA. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. If a student wishes to dispute a final grade, they should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If unresolved, they may file an appeal by submitting a Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five business days from the posting of the final grade. The Registrar's Office will inform the Dean’s Office, which may mediate or organize a panel review for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. ### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university acknowledges that students may experience exceptional circumstances, such as exceptional medical circumstances (including chronic illnesses), close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties, which may impact their ability to fulfill the expectations regarding attendance, assessment, and paying fees. 

To accommodate these students, the university expects them to submit appropriate documentation and contact their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. For trips during the term, approval from the Office of the Dean and Deans of Students is required. Students must also be in good academic standing and not on probation to be excused from the class. 

Instructors are expected to outline attendance expectations at the beginning of each term and handle individual cases of absence with flexibility. In cases where students must be absent due to an emergency but are unable to communicate their condition, emergency situations are considered part of exceptional circumstances.

For university-sponsored events, faculty or supervising staff can request an Excused Absence form on behalf of the student, ensuring that the Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office are informed for record-keeping purposes.

The university's approach emphasizes the responsibility of students to communicate with their instructors and provide necessary documentation, while also requiring instructors to be flexible and accommodating in these situations. The university's policies aim to support students in maintaining their academic progress despite facing exceptional circumstances.

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students at Fulbright University Vietnam are allowed to use generative AI tools like ChatGPT for their Capstone projects, but they must adhere to strict regulations outlined in the university's Code of Academic Integrity. The use of generative AI is subject to comprehensive documentation requirements. This documentation must include:

1. **Objective and Scope**: Clearly defining why generative AI is being used and how it contributes to the specific elements of the project.
2. **Tools and Platforms**: Specifying the AI tools, models, or platforms employed in the project.
3. **Process and Methodology**: Outlining how AI is incorporated into the project, detailing which aspects are generated, improved, or altered by AI.
4. **Ethical and Copyright Issues**: Addressing ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and detailing how these issues will be managed throughout the project.

Furthermore, students must ensure that any content generated by AI is properly attributed and not presented as their own original work. Failure to comply with these regulations can result in failure of the Capstone project. The university provides a detailed timeline and process for Capstone projects, including proposal submission, portfolio submission, and defense, which must be followed diligently.

The university's website and handbook also offer resources and guidelines for the Institutional Review Board (IRB) approval process, which may be relevant depending on the nature of the Capstone project. The use of generative AI in academic work at Fulbright University Vietnam is thus governed by a clear set of rules designed to ensure academic integrity and ethical conduct.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

Students working on projects related to mental health can get support through various means as outlined in the given contexts. Specifically, they can work with an additional non-academic advisor such as a mental health practitioner. These advisors can provide guidance, expertise, and support throughout the project development and implementation phases. Additionally, the resources listed include a Mental Health First Aid Training Program, a Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, a Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes, a Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services, and a Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Program. Each of these resources can offer different forms of support, from training and education to direct service provision and community engagement. Furthermore, the Capstone by Applied Project requires a final Evaluation Report that should demonstrate the project’s relevance to psychological principles and its potential or observed impact on mental health. This report should also include documentation of the student’s involvement and implementation of the program, providing insights or recommendations for future application or research. This structured approach ensures that students receive comprehensive support, not only from academic advisors but also from mental health professionals and community resources, ensuring the projects are well-informed, impactful, and beneficial to the community. The support system is designed to help students navigate the complexities of mental health issues and to ensure their projects are both academically rigorous and practically beneficial.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

After completing an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, students who wish to pursue a graduate program should first research and identify suitable graduate schools and programs that match their academic interests and career goals. They can utilize various resources available both on and off campus to facilitate this process:

1. **Academic Advisors and Major Advisors**: These individuals can provide guidance on graduate school options, application processes, and requirements specific to the desired field of study.

2. **Career Services Center**: Fulbright likely has a career services center that offers workshops, counseling sessions, and resources to help students prepare for graduate school applications, including resume and personal statement reviews.

3. **Libraries and Online Databases**: The university library and online databases can be invaluable resources for researching graduate programs, finding scholarship opportunities, and accessing academic journals and publications relevant to the student's field of interest.

4. **Graduate School Fairs and Information Sessions**: Attending graduate school fairs and information sessions can provide students with direct access to representatives from various graduate programs, who can offer insights into their programs and answer questions.

5. **Online Platforms and Resources**: Websites like GradSchools.com, Peterson's, and the official websites of graduate schools provide comprehensive information on programs, application requirements, and financial aid options.

6. **Professional Associations**: Joining professional associations related to the student's field of study can offer networking opportunities and information on graduate programs and scholarships.

7. **Fulbright Alumni Network**: Reaching out to Fulbright alumni who have pursued graduate studies can provide personal insights and advice on the process.

8. **Peterson's Graduate and Professional Directory**: This is a well-known resource for comprehensive information on graduate programs, including application requirements and deadlines.

9. **Financial Aid Office**: The financial aid office can provide information on funding opportunities for graduate studies, including fellowships, assistantships, and loans.

10. **Office of the Registrar**: The office of the registrar can assist with official transcripts and other necessary paperwork for graduate school applications.

Students should start this process well in advance of their intended graduate school start date to allow ample time for applications, securing financial aid, and making informed decisions about their future academic and career paths. It's important to tailor the resources used to the specific needs and goals of the individual student.

### Question 86: Can you give me information about teaching assistant program right now?  
### Answer: 

The teaching assistant program is a structured educational experience designed to support students in their academic and professional development. It typically involves a combination of coursework, practical experience, and mentorship. Here are some key aspects of a teaching assistant program based on the general information provided:

1. **Eligibility Criteria**: Students who wish to become teaching assistants usually need to meet certain academic requirements, such as a minimum GPA, completion of specific courses, and sometimes prior teaching experience or training.

2. **Allocation of Advisor**: Students are often assigned an advisor or mentor who helps guide them through the program, provides feedback on their teaching performance, and assists with professional development.

3. **The Advising Process**: The advising process involves regular meetings between the teaching assistant and their advisor to discuss progress, address any concerns, and plan for future development. Advisors may also provide resources and training opportunities.

4. **Project Format**: Teaching assistants may be involved in a variety of projects, such as leading discussion sections, grading assignments, developing teaching materials, and sometimes even designing and delivering their own lectures or workshops.

5. **Group Projects**: In some cases, teaching assistants may work in groups to co-teach a course or to collaborate on developing teaching materials. This can provide valuable experience in teamwork and collaborative learning.

6. **Capstone I and Capstone II**: Some programs may have a structured sequence of experiences, with "Capstone I" and "Capstone II" representing stages of increasing responsibility and complexity in teaching roles.

7. **IRB Approval**: If the teaching assistant's work involves human subjects research, they may need to obtain Institutional Review Board (IRB) approval to ensure the ethical treatment of participants.

8. **Academic Integrity**: Teaching assistants are expected to uphold high standards of academic integrity, both in their own work and in their interactions with students.

9. **Grading Process**: Teaching assistants often participate in the grading process, which can include developing rubrics, assigning grades, and providing feedback to students.

10. **Dissemination**: At the end of the program, teaching assistants may be encouraged to disseminate their teaching experiences and any innovations they have developed through presentations, publications, or other means.

It's important to note that the specifics of a teaching assistant program can vary significantly depending on the institution, department, and individual program design. The information provided here is a general overview and may not cover all the nuances of a particular teaching assistant program. For detailed and specific information, one should refer to the official guidelines and policies of the institution offering the program.

### Question 87: Where can I get the assist for internship?  
### Answer: 

The capstone program provides access to industry mentors who may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. These industry mentors could serve as secondary advisors or participate in the capstone panel, potentially assisting with grading. They are there to provide guidance and support relevant to industry practices, which could be invaluable for an internship. However, it's important to maintain regular communication with your primary advisor and follow the program's guidelines for meetings and submissions to ensure you're meeting the program's expectations and receiving the full benefit of the support offered.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get the information of campus usage for events so that you can have a proper place to study without getting interrupted, you should follow these steps:

1. **Check the University Calendar**: Most universities have an online calendar where they list all the events happening on campus. This is a good starting point to see if there are any events scheduled during the time you plan to study.

2. **Contact the Event Coordinator**: If you know the name of the event or the organization hosting it, you can contact the event coordinator directly to inquire about the event schedule and the space it will occupy.

3. **Visit the Registrar’s Office**: The Registrar’s Office often has a detailed schedule of all university events and may be able to provide you with a calendar or access to an online system where you can check event schedules.

4. **Use the University’s Online Booking System**: Many universities have an online system where student organizations can book spaces for events. Accessing this system might give you insight into where events are being held.

5. **Check with the Department or Building Administrators**: If you have a preference for a specific building or department, contacting the administrator of that area can provide you with information on upcoming events that might affect your study space.

6. **Subscribe to University Newsletters**: Some universities send out newsletters or emails with updates on campus events. Subscribing to these can keep you informed about potential disruptions.

7. **Ask the Student Life Office**: The Student Life Office often has a comprehensive view of student activities and can provide guidance on how to find out about event schedules.

Remember, it's important to plan your study schedule around known events to minimize disruptions. If you're unable to avoid an event, consider studying in quieter areas of the campus, such as the library, or during times when events are less likely to occur. Always be respectful of the event organizers and attendees, and understand that while you have a right to study, others have a right to host events on campus as well.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal. Fulbright will not evaluate transferable credit prior to acceptance. Transferable credit is determined after a student enrolls. Please read the Transfer Credit Policy V1.0 published in the One-Stop portal prior to submitting a request. An official transcript with seal from the issuing institution must be sent directly to the Office of the Registrar at the email registrar@fulbright.edu.vn or the mailing address in the Policy.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of CWP (Capstone Writing Project) include the following:

1. **Rubric for Final Reports**: The evaluation of the final reports is based on a structured rubric that assesses various aspects of the project, such as clarity, organization, methodology, analysis, and conclusions. The rubric is divided into criteria, each with equal weight, and scores range from 0.0 to 10.0. A score of 70% to 89.9% is required to achieve a Pass grade, while a score of 90% or above can result in a Pass with Honor grade.

2. **Public Defense**: Students are required to present their Capstone project in a public defense, which is evaluated by a capstone panel consisting of at least three members, including the advisor(s). The evaluation rubric for the public presentation also has criteria with equal weight, and the scores are also used to determine the final grade.

3. **Weighted Scoring**: The final scores are computed with a specific weight distribution:
   - Advisor(s) score: 40%
   - Independent reviewer score: 30%
   - Capstone panel score: 30%

4. **Grading**: The grading system is binary, with Pass and No Pass as the primary outcomes. A Pass grade is awarded for scores between 70% and 89.9%, while Pass with Honor is awarded for scores of 90% or above.

5. **Exceptional Cases**: In exceptional cases where the project demonstrates significant achievement, the capstone project can be awarded a Pass with Honor grade.

These policies ensure a comprehensive and fair evaluation process for the Capstone Writing Project, taking into account both the written report and the oral presentation. The involvement of multiple evaluators, including the advisor(s), helps to provide a balanced and rigorous assessment of the students' work.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you may have special considerations for your schedule due to your athletic commitments. Here are some strategies you might consider to potentially bypass physical education courses required to graduate:

1. **Consult with Academic Advising**: Reach out to your academic advisor to discuss your unique situation as a student athlete. They may be able to provide guidance on how to navigate the requirements.

2. **Credit for Athletic Participation**: Some universities offer credit for athletic participation, which can sometimes be used to fulfill physical education requirements. Check with your athletic department to see if this is an option.

3. **Alternative Courses**: Look for alternative courses that could fulfill the physical education requirement. For example, if you're involved in a sport that's not typically covered by the university's physical education offerings, you might be able to propose a course that aligns with your athletic experience.

4. **Petition Process**: If none of the above options work, you may need to go through a petition process to request an exemption from the physical education requirement. This usually involves providing documentation of your athletic participation and demonstrating how it meets the educational objectives of the physical education courses.

5. **Make-Up Options**: If you're unable to bypass the requirement, consider making up the physical education credits through other means, such as additional courses or approved activities that the university recognizes.

6. **Time Management**: Effective time management is crucial. Work closely with your coaches and academic advisors to ensure that your athletic and academic schedules are balanced.

7. **Review University Policies**: Familiarize yourself with the university's policies regarding physical education requirements and exemptions for student athletes. Each institution may have different rules and procedures.

8. **Stay Informed**: Keep yourself updated on any changes to university policies or new programs that might accommodate student athletes more effectively.

Remember, while it's important to manage your academic and athletic commitments, it's also crucial to ensure that you're meeting the educational requirements for graduation. Always approach these situations with honesty and transparency, and be prepared to provide any necessary documentation to support your case.

It's important to note that the specific policies and procedures for bypassing physical education requirements can vary significantly from one institution to another. Therefore, it's essential to consult directly with the relevant offices at your university, such as the athletic department, academic advising, and registrar's office, to understand the best course of action for your situation.

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

The policy for returning to the university dormitory and financial support would depend on the specific policies of the university you are attending. Generally, universities may have a limited number of spaces in their dormitories and may prioritize first-year students or students who have previously lived in the dorms but left due to legitimate reasons.

To find out if you can return to the dormitory, you should contact the Residential Life or Housing Office at your university. They will be able to provide you with the specific procedures and any available spaces.

Regarding financial support, some universities may offer financial aid or assistance for students who are experiencing housing difficulties. This could include grants, loans, or work-study opportunities to help with housing costs. However, the availability and amount of financial support would depend on the university's financial aid policies and your individual financial need.

To proceed, you should:

1. Contact the Residential Life Office to inquire about availability and the process for re-applying for dormitory housing.
2. Complete any necessary paperwork, such as the exit checklist and any application forms for returning to the dormitory.
3. Apply for financial aid if you believe you may need additional support to cover housing costs.
4. If you are granted a return to the dormitory, ensure you understand the terms of your stay, including any fees or conditions.
5. If you are facing financial hardship, reach out to the Financial Aid Office to discuss your situation and explore potential support options.

Remember to provide any documentation that may support your case, such as proof of your search for alternative housing and any financial statements that demonstrate your need for assistance.

In summary, while there is no universal answer, you should contact the relevant university offices to understand your options for returning to the dormitory and accessing financial support. Each case is considered individually, and the university staff will guide you through the process based on their policies and available resources.

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

Students can apply for funding from FUV or from other sources to fund the purchases of necessary chemicals/equipment for their capstone projects. The same process can be applied for club activities. Here are the steps to request funds for club activities:

1. **Research Funding Opportunities**: Look for available funding sources within FUV, such as the student research fund, or external grants and scholarships that support student clubs and activities.

2. **Prepare a Proposal**: Develop a detailed proposal outlining the purpose of the funding request, the budget breakdown, and how the funds will be used to benefit the club and its members. Include a timeline for the activities and expected outcomes.

3. **Submit the Proposal**: Submit the proposal to the appropriate office within FUV, such as the Office of Student Affairs or the Financial Aid Office, depending on the specific funding source.

4. **Follow Up**: After submission, follow up with the office to ensure they have received the proposal and to inquire about the review process and timeline.

5. **Attend Meetings**: Be prepared to attend meetings with the review committee to discuss the proposal in more detail and answer any questions they may have.

6. **Receive Feedback**: Be open to feedback and be willing to revise the proposal as necessary to strengthen the application.

7. **Approval and Disbursement**: If the proposal is approved, the funds will be disbursed according to the agreed-upon terms and conditions.

8. **Reporting and Accountability**: Once the funds are received, maintain records of how the funds are spent and be prepared to provide reports on the use of the funds and the outcomes of the club activities.

9. **Communication**: Keep the club members informed about the funding process and the use of the funds to maintain transparency and trust within the club.

It's important to note that securing funding can be competitive, so a well-prepared and compelling proposal is crucial. Also, the process may involve significant paperwork, including applications, budget spreadsheets, and possibly legal agreements regarding the use of the funds.

In summary, students should research available funding sources, prepare a detailed proposal, submit it to the appropriate office, follow up on the application, be prepared to discuss the proposal, and be accountable for the use of the funds once they are received.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are several ways provided by the university to get support in your academic path. Firstly, students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work. Additionally, support will be provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary. Mentorship and industry involvement are also available, with industry mentors potentially serving as secondary advisors for capstone projects or participating in grading as members of the capstone panel. Furthermore, projects will have access to limited funding for materials and resources, with policies on budgeting and purchasing provided. Lastly, students can work with faculty to find alternative sources for equipment and chemicals if they are not available, apply for funding from the university or other sources, or adjust their experimental design if necessary. These various support mechanisms are designed to help students navigate their academic journey, overcome unexpected setbacks, and successfully complete their projects.

### Question 95: Can you give me the information about student fees and charges policy?  
### Answer: 

In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Students should be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if resulting in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment.

EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. ### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

If you're experiencing issues with a professor's teaching methods and believe they do not meet academic standards, it's important to address the situation in a constructive and appropriate manner. Here are steps you can take:

1. **Document the Issues**: Keep a detailed record of the incidents that you find problematic. Note the dates, specifics of the incidents, and any relevant details that could help support your concerns.

2. **Meet with the Professor**: Schedule a meeting with the professor to discuss your concerns. Approach the conversation professionally and calmly, focusing on specific examples rather than general complaints. This can often resolve the issue directly.

3. **Consult with Your Academic Advisor**: Share your concerns with your academic advisor. They can offer advice, mediate discussions, and provide support. They may also have insights into the professor's teaching style and expectations.

4. **Contact the Department Chair**: If the issue is not resolved through the initial steps, you can reach out to the department chair. Explain your concerns, providing the documented evidence you've gathered. The department chair can investigate the matter further and take appropriate action.

5. **File an Academic Grievance**: If the issue remains unresolved and significantly impacts your academic experience, you may need to file an academic grievance. This process varies by institution, but generally involves submitting a formal complaint to a designated office (such as the Office of Academic Affairs or the Dean's Office). Follow your institution's specific procedures for filing a grievance.

6. **Seek Support from Student Affairs**: Student Affairs offices often provide support and guidance for students facing academic issues. They can offer advice, mediate discussions, and sometimes intervene on behalf of students.

7. **Review Institutional Policies**: Familiarize yourself with your institution's policies on academic standards, student rights, and grievance procedures. Understanding these policies can help you navigate the process more effectively.

8. **Consider External Resources**: If the issue is severe and you feel your academic and personal well-being are at risk, consider seeking support from external resources such as counseling services or academic support centers.

Remember, it's important to approach the situation professionally and with a focus on resolving the issue rather than seeking retribution. The goal is to ensure a positive and productive academic experience for yourself and other students.

APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

You should go to your academic advisor for advice on whether to pursue a Capstone project. They can provide personalized guidance based on your interests, academic performance, and post-graduation plans. Additionally, you can consult with potential primary advisors within the History department to discuss your project ideas and get their input. If you're unsure about the research aspect, consider discussing your concerns with them to see if they can help alleviate your worries or suggest alternative paths to achieving your academic and career goals. Remember, the Capstone project is a significant commitment and should be undertaken if you are passionate about historical research and have the time and interest to dedicate to it. If you're not particularly interested in research, it might be more beneficial to focus on other aspects of your academic performance, such as coursework and GPA, which can also contribute to graduating with distinction.

seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

If you are a Fulbright student and need to request an absence due to participation in a sponsored academic event like a basketball tournament, you should follow these steps:

1. **Discuss with Your Instructor(s):** As soon as you know about the tournament, discuss your planned absence with your course instructors. Provide them with as much notice as possible (at least 24 hours prior to class time).

2. **Complete the Excused Absence Form:** Contact your instructor(s) to complete the Excused Absence form. This form is necessary to document your absence and ensure it is recognized as excused.

3. **Academic Affairs Team:** If you need further assistance or have any issues with the process, contact the Academic Affairs team at ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn. They can provide guidance and support in completing the necessary paperwork and ensuring your absence is properly documented.

4. **Proof of Attendance:** Prepare to provide proof of your attendance at the tournament, such as an acceptance letter, invitation, or any other relevant documentation.

5. **Proof of Travel:** Also, prepare to show proof of your travel arrangements, such as your flight and accommodation information or itinerary.

6. **Reflection Paper:** After the tournament, write a reflection paper (300-500 words) about your experience and submit it to ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn.

7. **Transcript Request:** For the official transcript, you should contact the Registrar’s Office. They can guide you on the process and requirements for obtaining an official transcript.

Remember, it's important to follow the university's procedures and provide all necessary documentation to ensure your absence is properly excused and to avoid any issues with your academic record.

### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

To borrow books from the library, follow these steps:

1. **Obtain a Library Card**: If you don't already have one, visit the library to apply for a library card. You'll typically need to provide proof of identity and residence.

2. **Locate the Books**: Use the library's catalog to search for the books you need. Libraries often have online catalogs accessible through their website.

3. **Check Availability**: Once you've found the books you want, check their availability. Some books might be on loan or reserved by others.

4. **Borrow the Books**: If the books are available, you can borrow them at the library's circulation desk. You'll need to present your library card and may need to sign them out.

5. **Understand Loan Periods and Limits**: Each library has its own loan periods and limits on the number of books you can borrow at a time. Be sure to familiarize yourself with these rules.

6. **Renew Books**: Most libraries allow you to renew books online, by phone, or in person before the due date. Renewing extends the loan period.

7. **Return Books**: Return the books on time to avoid late fees. Some libraries have book drops for convenience, while others require you to return books at the circulation desk.

8. **Use Library Resources**: Besides borrowing physical books, many libraries offer access to digital resources, databases, and e-books that you can use remotely.

9. **Contact Library Staff**: If you have any questions or issues, don't hesitate to ask library staff for assistance.

Remember, borrowing policies can vary between different libraries, so it's always a good idea to check with your local library for specific rules and procedures.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

The major report, in this context, is the Evaluation Report. To work effectively with this report, one must adhere to the outlined structure and content requirements. Here's a step-by-step guide on how to approach each section:

**A. Executive Summary (5%)**
- **Conciseness:** Write a brief overview that captures the essence of the project. This should include the objectives, methods used, and anticipated impact.
- **Clarity:** Clearly state the project's purpose and its expected contributions to psychology or applied mental health.
- **Structure:** Start with a brief introduction to the project, followed by a summary of the objectives, methods, and expected outcomes.

**B. Rationale (10%)**
- **Theoretical Foundation:** Clearly articulate the psychological and theoretical underpinnings of the project. This involves explaining why the chosen objectives are significant and how they relate to existing psychological concepts.
- **Significance:** Establish the relevance of the project to the field of psychology or applied mental health. This could involve discussing gaps in the literature that your project aims to address.
- **Linkage:** Make a clear connection between the theoretical concepts and the applied goals of the project.

**Mapping to Learning Outcomes (MLOs and CLOs):**
- **MLO1 & MLO2:** These outcomes focus on applying psychological principles and interpreting/designing research. The Executive Summary and Rationale sections require the student to demonstrate these skills through effective communication of objectives, methods, and findings.
- **MLO3:** This outcome emphasizes incorporating sociocultural factors in scientific inquiry. The student should consider how sociocultural factors influence the project's objectives and findings.
- **MLO5:** This outcome involves applying self-reflection and project management skills. The Evaluation Report requires the student to manage the project's objectives, methods, and findings effectively.
- **CLOs:** The report also maps to the Course Learning Outcomes (CLOs), particularly CLO1 (articulate and justify project objectives, methods, and findings), CLO2 (effective communication through various media), and CLO3 (application of ethical standards and project management skills).

**Communication Methods:**
- **Written:** The Evaluation Report itself is a written document. It should be well-structured, clear, and concise.
- **Visual:** Consider including charts, graphs, or diagrams to visually represent data or processes. This can enhance understanding and make complex information more accessible.
- **Oral:** If the report is to be presented orally, prepare a clear and engaging presentation that summarizes the key points of the report. This could be part of a class presentation or a defense of the project.

**Ethical Considerations:**
- Ensure that the Evaluation Report adheres to ethical standards, particularly if the project involved human subjects. This aligns with MLO4 and CLO4.

**Project Management:**
- Reflect on the project management skills used throughout the project lifecycle, including planning, execution, monitoring, and closure. This self-reflection is crucial for MLO5.

**Self-Reflection:**
- Conclude the report with a self-reflection section where you critically evaluate your own performance, learning, and growth throughout the project. This demonstrates the application of MLO5.

**Overall, the Evaluation Report is a comprehensive document that requires the student to synthesize their project work, communicate effectively, and reflect on their learning and skills development.** It is a critical component of the assessment process, demonstrating the student's ability to apply psychological principles and research methods in a real-world context.

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

For Class of 2024 students, they need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulfill their Exploratory requirements, one course from each category, with at most 4 out of 16 credits counted as Pass/No Pass. For students of classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027, they need to complete 32 credits (8 courses), eight credits from each category, to fulfill their Exploratory requirements.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and passions lie. Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. and passions lie. Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. Notes: • Class of 2023 students are exempted from the Exploratory requirements. • There are four exploratory categories for the students of classes of 2024, 2025, 2026, and 2027: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing. • Class of 2024 students need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulfill their Exploratory requirements, one course from each

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 12]
limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. Notes: •  Class of 2023 students are exempted from the Exploratory requirements. • There are four exploratory categories for the students of classes of 2024, 2025, 2026, and 2027: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing. • Class of 2024 students need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulﬁll their Exploratory requirements, one course from each category, with at most 4 out of 16 credits counted as Pass/No Pass. • Students of classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027 need to complete 32 credits (8 courses), eight credits from each category, to fulﬁll their Exploratory requirements. Elec8ve and Experien8al Learning Requirements Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue.
